               <div class="pop-out Op-0" style="content:;position:absolute;border-style:solid;border-top-width:0;border-bottom-width:8px;border-left-width:7px;border-right-width:7px;border-color:white transparent;display:block;height:0;width:0;z-index:2147483647;top:30px;left:50%;margin-left:-7px;transition-property:opacity;transition-duration:0.1s;transition-timing-function:linear;pointer-events:none;">
               </div>
               <div class="pop-out Op-0" style="content:;position:absolute;border-style:solid;border-top-width:0;border-bottom-width:9px;border-left-width:8px;border-right-width:8px;border-color:#e7e7e7 transparent;display:block;height:0;width:0;z-index:2147483646;top:29px;left:50%;margin-left:-8px;transition-property:opacity;transition-duration:0.1s;transition-timing-function:linear;pointer-events:none;">
               </div>
               <div class="pop-out Op-0" style="position:absolute;overflow:hidden;margin-top:-3px;margin-left:-28.5px;top:40px;left:50%;right:;display:inline-block;transition-property:opacity;transition-duration:0.1s;transition-timing-function:linear;pointer-events:none;">
                <div style="position:relative;background-color:white;-webkit-border-radius:5px;-moz-border-radius:5px;-khtml-border-radius:5px;border-radius:5px;border:solid 1px #e7e7e7;padding:4px;z-index:2147483645;">
                 <div style="width:47px;height:20px;">
                  <iframe allowtransparency="true" frameborder="0" scrolling="no" src="//www.facebook.com/plugins/like.php?href=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.facebook.com%2FYahooTravel&amp;width=47&amp;layout=button&amp;action=like&amp;show_faces=false&amp;share=false&amp;height=20" style="border:none;overflow:hidden;width:47px;height:35px;">
                  </iframe>
                 </div>
                </div>
               </div>
              </div>
             </div>
             <div class="Pos-r D-ib Cur-d Va-t" style="height:40px;">
              <div class="D-ib" style="height:40px;padding:0 11.5px;">
               <a class="D-ib" href="https://www.twitter.com/YahooTravel" rel="me" target="_blank">
                <i class="Icon Fw-n Va-t" style="color:#00aceb;height:40px;line-height:40px;font-size:16px;">
                 
                </i>
               </a>
               <div class="pop-out Op-0" style="content:;position:absolute;border-style:solid;border-top-width:0;border-bottom-width:8px;border-left-width:7px;border-right-width:7px;border-color:white transparent;display:block;height:0;width:0;z-index:2147483647;top:30px;left:50%;margin-left:-7px;transition-property:opacity;transition-duration:0.1s;transition-timing-function:linear;pointer-events:none;">
               </div>
               <div class="pop-out Op-0" style="content:;position:absolute;border-style:solid;border-top-width:0;border-bottom-width:9px;border-left-width:8px;border-right-width:8px;border-color:#e7e7e7 transparent;display:block;height:0;width:0;z-index:2147483646;top:29px;left:50%;margin-left:-8px;transition-property:opacity;transition-duration:0.1s;transition-timing-function:linear;pointer-events:none;">
               </div>

                <div style="position:relative;background-color:white;-webkit-border-radius:5px;-moz-border-radius:5px;-khtml-border-radius:5px;border-radius:5px;border:solid 1px #e7e7e7;padding:4px;z-index:2147483645;">

                  </iframe>
                 </div>
                </div>
               </div>
              </div>
             </div>

                </i>
               </a>
               <div class="pop-out Op-0" style="content:;position:absolute;border-style:solid;border-top-width:0;border-bottom-width:8px;border-left-width:7px;border-right-width:7px;border-color:white transparent;display:block;height:0;width:0;z-index:2147483647;top:30px;left:50%;margin-left:-7px;transition-property:opacity;transition-duration:0.1s;transition-timing-function:linear;pointer-events:none;">

         <div class="Pos-r Z-0 article-container" data-template="desktop" id="article-88490438857" style="background-color:white;min-height:315px;">
          <div class="Pos-r sticky-container print-article" style="min-height:315px;">
           <div class="article-inner-container" style="max-width:1280px;">
            <div class="inset-container Mx-a">
             <div class="GridTable">
              <div class="D-tbr row-template">
               <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t col-left">
                <div class="content" style="width:825px;min-width:825px;">
                 <noscript>
                 </noscript>
                 <noscript>
                 </noscript>
                 <div class="GridTable grid-content">
                  <div class="D-tbr row-content">
                   <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t col-left Pend-20" style="width:305px;max-width:305px;">
                    <h1 class="Font-A-6-110 title W-100" id="article-aft-title-88490438857">
                     Sea Lions and Ostriches and Whales  Oh Yes! 8 Animal Adventures Along the Pacific Coast
                    </h1>
                    <div class="attribution-component D-b W-100" id="article-aft-attribution-88490438857" style="max-width:305px;">
                     <div class="author-info author-info-text-first Pt-10 W-100 Bd-t Bd-b Bdstart-0 Bdend-0">
                      <div class="GridTable W-100">
                       <div class="D-tbr">
                        <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t">
                         <cite class="byline col D-b Fs-n" style="padding-bottom:15px;">
                          <span class="author-name Font-C-2-140 D-b">
                           <a class="attribution-name Font-C-2-140 Fw-b Whs-n" data-ylk="t1:a2;t2:article;t3:cat;t8:ce1ec421-4bf3-3927-8738-6011315ddbf7;t9:17;elm:itm;elmt:link;itc:0" href="https://twitter.com/EBexplores" style="color:#000;" target="_blank">
                            Erica Bray
                           </a>
                          </span>
                          <time class="date Font-C-2-140 Fw-n D-b">
                           <span>
                            June 12, 2014
                           </span>
                          </time>
                         </cite>
                        </div>
                       </div>
                      </div>
                     </div>
                    </div>
                   </div>
                   <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t col-right" style="max-width:500px;">
                    <div class="text-body-wrapper W-100 Font-B-1-160">
                     <noscript>
                     </noscript>
                     <div class="text-body W-100 Font-B-1-160" id="article-aft-text-body-88490438857" style="color:#222222;max-width:500px;">
                      <div class="body read-more-cut">
                       <div class="pre-cut" style="height:auto;margin-bottom:1.5em;">
                        <p>
                         <img alt="Sea Lions and Ostriches and Whales  Oh Yes! 8 Animal Adventures Along the Pacific Coast" height="335" src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w500/ad9414edcedf1f5f89f99d0fabbe64203c6e7dad.jpg" width="500"/>
                        </p>
                        <p>
                         <em>
                          Heceta Head Lighthouse on the Oregon coast. (Photo: iStock/Thinkstock)
                         </em>
                        </p>
                        <p>
                         Driving down the Oregon and California coasts its hard to keep your eyes on the road  the scenery is that spectacular. Highways 101 and 1 hug rugged oceanfront cliffs, roll past pastoral farmland, and weave through redwood forests, vineyards, and beach communities.
                        </p>
                        <p>
                         And yet, epic scenes arent the only attention grabbers: Animals constantly vied for my attention. And Im not talking about the wander-into-the-middle-of-the-road-and-force-you-to-jam-the-brakes kind either. Here, amid large expanses of natural settings, where I might be the only car for miles and miles, I found myself consistently pulling over to watch sheep grazing, birds migrating and cows well, being cows.
                        </p>
                        <p>
                         Beyond these quiet observations, unique opportunities abounded to get up close with the regions awesome animals, like whales and sea lions. Heres eight of the best  including at least one of the
                         <em>
                          extinct
                         </em>
                         variety.
                        </p>
                        <p>
                         <iframe data-src="https://mapsengine.google.com/map/u/0/embed?mid=zyFTM0JPEA1s.kDm82L11pl5c" height="480" width="640">
                         </iframe>
                        </p>
                        <p>
                         <strong>
                          Depoe Bay, Oregon: Gray Whales
                         </strong>
                        </p>
                        <p>
                         The self-proclaimed Whale Watching Capital of the Oregon Coast, Depoe Bay welcomes pods of gray whales from March through December. Visitors can observe these gentle giants spouting in open water from the Whale Watch Center. For me, however, binoculars wouldnt cut it. For $18, I joined a one-hour boat ride with
                         <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:ce1ec421-4bf3-3927-8738-6011315ddbf7;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.tradewindscharters.com/" target="_blank">
                          Tradewinds Charters
                         </a>
                         and got the thrill of a lifetime when several whales spouted right in front of me.
                         <strong>
                          <img alt="A gray whale tail off the coast of Depoe Bay, Oregon" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w500/d168701c245e90ea7c6a3d14127a738f18c1c8de.jpg" height="304" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="500"/>
                         </strong>
                        </p>
                        <p>
                         <em>
                          A gray whale tail off the coast of Depoe Bay (Photo:
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:ce1ec421-4bf3-3927-8738-6011315ddbf7;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://www.flickr.com/photos/ocva/2699335172/in/photolist-57wNiA-57wMSC-55QDUR-7ASgwv-57sAjH-57wPS1-57sAep-57wNyG-57sFi8-57sALp-55PXfR-55PXkn-57wMYy-57sA7n-58Xfhb-57kozJ-57gdjH-7DBGGL-58i13Q-57dQmp-56M4tU-57wM3Y-57gcpt-55VZDL-55PX6p-576avb-7FXBEr-575W5q-571qvc-56Mtvo-7SejZ1-7SeiCU-58T3HH-57wmzs-57qTaD-574SYU-575aMN-57PihY-57wn1j-56JgU8" target="_blank" title="Gray Whale Tale">
                           OCVA/Flickr
                          </a>
                          )
                         </em>
                        </p>
                       </div>
                       <div class="post-cut W-100" id="post-cut" style="transition-property:none;-webkit-transition-property:none;transition-duration:10s;-webkit-transition-duration:10s;transition-timing-function:ease-in;-webkit-transition-timing-function:ease-in;overflow:hidden;max-height:0;max-width:500px;">
                        <p>
                         <strong>
                          Newport, Oregon: Sea Lions
                         </strong>
                        </p>
                        <p>
                         You hear them before you see them. While strolling the resort town of Newport, I followed the loud honking to a tiny pier dominated by sea lions. Sea lions are scattered up and down the west coast shoreline, but this is the closest that I got to them. And heres the kicker: I think some of them actually posed for my camera, in between barking, growling and, snuggling with one another.
                         <strong>
                          <img alt="Sea lions hanging out on the rocks in Newport, Oregon" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w500/bcdb0b6ec8a1e6a11dd7b23195932e3a12be2d85.jpg" height="331" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="500"/>
                         </strong>
                        </p>
                        <p>
                         <em>
                          Sea lions hang out on the rocks (Photo:
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:ce1ec421-4bf3-3927-8738-6011315ddbf7;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://www.flickr.com/photos/kightp/7830025514/in/photolist-cVUVMU-dY8kiN-7v5KED-bmd3Yg-bmd3Vv-61Kvqn-cVR9rd-8wH7f2-8wL6Jm-bmd4CK-eZPaLh-61Kun2-bmcxNT-61KueX-985SW5-61KuDi-8GPJq-h6GXkW-61PGG1-61KtP6-8t4jSf-8t1i82-8t4jVW-61Kuvv-61Kv1i-61Ku7k-bAXcdE-bPRQAt-61KvPk-61Kw5a-61KvFg-cVUW9W-61Kwfi-7a64TF-61KuTi-61Kvbe-61PH6Y-61PGrQ-61PEKC-7a9TKW-61Ktxp-61PHzU-61KtYM-7a64Y8-jVGjCc-5yTeUd-8GNkw-d5pyKL-cXYzCb-d5pysw" target="_blank">
                           Pat Knight/Flickr
                          </a>
                          )
                         </em>
                        </p>
                        <p>
                         <img alt="image" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w359/b3b5f6b94bb987ae7b9b0b7b5b586de1f7297cc4.jpg" height="478" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="359"/>
                        </p>
                        <p>
                         <em>
                          (Photo: iStock/Thinkstock)
                         </em>
                        </p>
                        <p>
                         <strong>
                          Port Orford, Oregon: Dinosaurs
                         </strong>
                        </p>
                        <p>
                         I was the oldest visitor without a child to journey back in time at
                         <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:ce1ec421-4bf3-3927-8738-6011315ddbf7;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.prehistoricgardens.com/" target="_blank">
                          Prehistoric Gardens
                         </a>
                          but I didnt care. The seven-year-old girl in me who used to be obsessed with dinosaurs was happy to pay the $10 admission and traverse remote forest trails where giant (albeit cartoonish) dinosaurs lurk.
                         <strong>
                          <img alt="Dinosaurs in Port Orford, Oregon" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w500/94a192fd37fcbe27638e9a2eb86835def7104c77.jpg" height="331" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="500"/>
                         </strong>
                        </p>
                        <p>
                         <em>
                          (Photo:
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:ce1ec421-4bf3-3927-8738-6011315ddbf7;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://www.flickr.com/photos/djwudi/4446615770/in/photolist-cd8yxG-cd8yqL-7LS6GX-bVLhnX-bVLhKM-cd8yXE-cd8yS9-cd8yau-6Wyiao-bVL6v6-7tE87c-7LW4X9-7LW4jY-7LW7Gq-6Wyids-6WyioA-bVLhRX-6Wui6c-6Wyirb-6Wyi8d" target="_blank">
                           Michael Hanscom/Flickr
                          </a>
                          )
                         </em>
                        </p>
                        <p>
                         <strong>
                          Klamath, California: Babe the Blue Ox
                         </strong>
                        </p>
                        <p>
                         Hes the stuff of legend. And at 35 feet tall, hes hard to miss from Highway 101. The loyal companion to Paul Bunyan, Babe guards the Redwood attraction
                         <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:ce1ec421-4bf3-3927-8738-6011315ddbf7;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.treesofmystery.net/paul-babe.php" target="_blank">
                          Trees of Mystery
                         </a>
                         and is always camera-ready.
                         <strong>
                          <img alt="Babe the Blue Ox in Klamath, California" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w500/c5ed0f8f6f25bb9e013387379760f7840fac99e2.jpg" height="375" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="500"/>
                         </strong>
                        </p>
                        <p>
                         <em>
                          (Photo:
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:ce1ec421-4bf3-3927-8738-6011315ddbf7;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://www.flickr.com/photos/mytravelphotos/6824795433/in/photolist-bp5TtP-aP3MDe-4U9SA-6apqY3-6aprK1-6aprtC-6jVod-6jVpe-6jVoY-6jVme-6jVn4-6jVpW-a7UXbZ-a7XQK9-a7XR57-a7UXQ2-a7UYK2-a7XQd5-6aprzA-6aprQN-6mFjap-7HtH94-bp5Shc-bp5RUM-bp5SQa-6mFjf4-6mKtqG-amZPNz-an3wYE-an3DS9-an3CEf-an3Avq-amZSGT-amZMHD-amZSgn-amZH14-amZTMn-an3E1Q-amZR5K-an3Drd-amZKTD-an3BJw-an3BgA-amZQvr-amZNHx-amZKHP-amZRJZ-6owxw4-6owxXc-6oAGF9" target="_blank">
                           Jasperdo/Flickr
                          </a>
                          )
                         </em>
                        </p>
                        <p>
                        </p>
                        <p>
                         <strong>
                          Monterey, California: Sea Otters
                         </strong>
                        </p>
                        <p>
                         While I spotted sea otters a few times along Monterey Countys shoreline, the most intimate encounter came at the world-famous
                         <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:ce1ec421-4bf3-3927-8738-6011315ddbf7;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.montereybayaquarium.org/" target="_blank">
                          Monterey Bay Aquarium
                         </a>
                         . I really wanted to take one home  especially after coming face-to-face with resident sea otters as they performed underwater gymnastics behind a giant glass enclosure flanked by mesmerized, cooing humans.
                         <strong>
                          <img alt="Sea otter at the Monterey Bay Aquarium in California" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w500/3543e813357f2a8c881fec5aca0784d9386ad560.jpg" height="333" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="500"/>
                         </strong>
                        </p>
                        <p>
                         <em>
                          A sea otter at the Monterey Bay Aquarium (Photo:
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:ce1ec421-4bf3-3927-8738-6011315ddbf7;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://www.flickr.com/photos/77043400@N00/849368068/in/photolist-5mczwQ-yTBf7-eEXhi6-7rMrFK-5abXdp-99uYgY-ahi4jW-3ekmg6-8bhcYu-8aQTGQ-2i4ex3-9cGRdc-DYLTz-3mH11p-2i4evy-2i4ezA-4xaJ8p-78DvGH-78HnCY-78Hnom" target="_blank">
                           Donna Sutton/Flickr
                          </a>
                          )
                         </em>
                        </p>
                        <p>
                         <strong>
                          Monterey, California: Sea gulls
                         </strong>
                        </p>
                        <p>
                         These birds arent exactly exotic nor are they rare, but they made lovely evening companions as I sipped wine at sunset at
                         <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:ce1ec421-4bf3-3927-8738-6011315ddbf7;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.atasteofmonterey.com/visit-monterey-wine-store" target="_blank">
                          A Taste of Monterey
                         </a>
                         .
                         <strong>
                          <img alt="Sea gull on the beach in Monterey, California" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w500/8075046654a48ff5553e0ea2f95b1bbfd52aba07.jpg" height="333" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="500"/>
                         </strong>
                        </p>
                        <p>
                         <em>
                          A sea gull perched near the beach (Photo:
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:ce1ec421-4bf3-3927-8738-6011315ddbf7;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://www.flickr.com/photos/chtyim/2977185586/in/photolist-5x5RxY-686pmY-5WnbQm-6PRP8b-9jgZcJ-683ra-hAKgYj-kZs24-gNepS3-dwxAAH-g8LUfX-g8MEUe-5mge5k-5AAhyg-67LMLn-4ywkGC-gk5ruE-xPB3f-xPAZS-7y5rZg" target="_blank">
                           Terrence Yim/Flickr
                          </a>
                          )
                         </em>
                        </p>
                        <p>
                         <strong>
                          San Simeon, California: Elephant Seals
                         </strong>
                        </p>
                        <p>
                         There are so many elephant seals scattered about at
                         <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:ce1ec421-4bf3-3927-8738-6011315ddbf7;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://sansimeonchamber.org/attractions/elephant-seals/" target="_blank">
                          Piedras Blancas rookery
                         </a>
                         , its easy to mistake it for a rocky beach. Nearly 17,000 call this spot home. Be sure to stick to the Elephant Seal Boardwalk overlooking the beach, as elephant seals can get aggressive, especially if you try mimicking their mating call.
                         <strong>
                          <img alt="Elephant seals on the beach in San Simeon, California" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w500/8bad83632d07be6d56e7189b611dea95093a0059.jpg" height="333" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="500"/>
                         </strong>
                        </p>
                        <p>
                         <em>
                          Elephant seals on the beach (Photo:
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:ce1ec421-4bf3-3927-8738-6011315ddbf7;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://www.flickr.com/photos/jlodder/8217716665/in/photolist-huVCph-9CSUMt-htuEMt-dFRHPZ-9mhXob-cBVEqL-9mefuv-7zLci8-5RwCZn-9me9kz-565gn7-hiEZCq-hh8zuR-7APPDm-7AL3Bn-7uRDqn-5JrNMQ-94q53c-833NWL-94q5aM-7ur7Se-dJ6XUj-gDv6aq-8Ydm8S-94q58x-94tawU-dwaWS6-5UwyxA-iTWJsi-9KHpxv-dJ7YFb-9eLwb9-jh7S-bQXT4T-7tuUSQ-7vd8Fz-htuyyB-3dXw3o-htvLp7-9iKjzN-dRgk66-bSJh96-35WRyj-htvX8F-3dT5CV-94q57k-94tanE-35tL5z-35tKFM-7n2Sk" target="_blank">
                           John Lodder/Flickr
                          </a>
                          )
                         </em>
                        </p>
                        <p>
                         <strong>
                          Solvang, California: Ostriches
                         </strong>
                        </p>
                        <p>
                         These eight-foot-tall birds arent indigenous to California, but a visit to
                         <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:ce1ec421-4bf3-3927-8738-6011315ddbf7;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://www.ostrichlandusa.com/" target="_blank">
                          OstrichLand USA
                         </a>
                         put me face-to-face with the flightless creatures. For $5 (admission plus a bowl of food), I got to feed the flock. Just dont let their long eyelashes fool you: These birds are aggressive and attack the food tin with gusto  hold on tight!
                         <img alt="Solvang, California: Ostriches" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w500/dd5f7fd5d9152c87396848ba813d438d7e86701f.jpg" height="333" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="500"/>
                        </p>
                        <p>
                         <em>
                          (Photo:
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:ce1ec421-4bf3-3927-8738-6011315ddbf7;t9:18;itc:0" href="https://www.flickr.com/photos/averain/7890677790/in/photolist-eiSPtp-d2gMAN-d2ghWS-d2gswo-d2gKzw-d2gFWS-d2gEnj-d2gB99-82K5tK-d2gCNf-d2gHL7-k8AMRv-k8BVvr-k8CtS1-k8BW5o-k8zSL4-k8A5t2-k8A1pF-k8AB5k-k8zYWk-k8AM7K-k8A3pc-k8zR3e-k8CA5w-k8CCmf-eNMYfa-eNZti3-eNZxE5-eNZwDj-eNZumj-eNZvoC-eNN9rM-eNNf6H-eNZDNW-eNNd6B-eNNc3X-eNZApj-5rh12s-5rcPhV-gnY5oK-gnXxBW-gnXLjR-gnXx7Y-gnXxTs-gnXKPT-j8cxY-j8cG4-j8cvS-j8cPW-j8cLS" target="_blank">
                           Justin Ennis/Flickr
                          </a>
                          )
                         </em>
                        </p>
                        <p>
                         <em>
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:ce1ec421-4bf3-3927-8738-6011315ddbf7;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://deepexhale.com/?page_id=2" target="_blank">
                           Erica Bray
                          </a>
                          is a travel marketing consultant, writer and yoga teacher based in Chicago. She does a handstand everywhere she travels, a tradition shes been honoring since the age of 19  even risking arrest in some cases.
                         </em>
                        </p>
                       </div>

world\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E), even though its rare for visitors to actually catch a glimpse of the big, spotted cats. These trails lead to several \u003Cspan style=\"color: blue;\"\u003Ewaterfalls\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E as well as the summit of Victoria Peak, the highest peak in Belize. Skyscanner survey\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#xA0;found that&#xA0;only one percent of people actually prefer the middle seat on a plane. No surprise there. But Frontier Airlines may change all that.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe budget airline plans to stop the middle seat haters with its new 19-inch middle seats, according to \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.cntraveler.com\u002Fstories\u002F2015-07-09\u002Fthe-one-airline-that-s-actually-improving-the-middle-seat\"\u003Ecntraveler.com\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. That size is one inch wider than Frontier&#x2019;s window and aisle seats and, the airline claims, wider than on any other U.S. airline.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAnother bonus? Frontier does not plan to charge more for the wider middle seats.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ESound too good to be true? It&#x2019;s not: There are downsides. The seats will have less padding; passengers in these seats will be closer to the seat in front of them and behind them (less pitch), which affects legroom; and the seats do not recline (though Frontier calls them&#xA0;&#x201C;pre-reclined&#x201D;).&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ETo avoid all these pitfalls, a traveler would still have to purchase&#xA0;a middle seat in the more expensive premium economy &#x201C;Stretch&#x201D; section.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Ftravel\u002Fthe-new-airline-seat-that-turns-economy-into-business-101370413642.html\"\u003EThe New Airline Seat That Turns Economy Into Business Class\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EPerhaps the inch of extra room in the middle seat is to offset some of the other changes coming to Frontier. According to cntraveler.com, this year the airline is adding 12 seats to every Airbus A320 and A319 it flies. It&#x2019;s also set to be the first U.S. airline to put a 186-seat A320 into service, which has an extra six seats, thanks to smaller bathrooms.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBut Frontier isn&#x2019;t worried about that:&#xA0;&quot;Customers fly on regional aircraft all the time when they can&#x2019;t stand up in the lavatory,&#x201C;says Daniel Shurz, chief commercial officer for Frontier. &quot;They handle that just fine.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EWATCH: Flying Singapore Airlines in First Class for an Hour Ruined My Life\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-embed tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Ciframe width=\"540\" height=\"303\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fscreen.yahoo.com\u002Fa-broad-abroad\u002Ffirst-class-broad-abroad-181008113.html?format=embed\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fiframe\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ELet Yahoo Travel inspire you every day. Greenlands Finest Microbrew Beers","summary":"I'm a beer woman. So on my trip to Greenland, when I heard there was a craft brewery in town, I made a beeline for it.","body":"\u003Cp\u003EAnybody who knows me knows I don&#x2019;t drink vodka. I don&#x2019;t do tequila. And I&#x2019;ve never been a big fan of anything that comes with a garnish. I am, however, a beer girl. Raised in Cincinnati, a town with German roots, I have a deep love of hops, and over the years my tastes have been refined from \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fhudepohlbeer.com\u002F\"\u003EHudepohl\u003C\u002Fa\u003E and Schlitz to craft beers. Don&#x2019;t get me wrong &#x2014; when stuck on a riverboat for a bachelorette party in, say, Austin, Texas (thanks to my sister Emily), I will still happily down a Bud, a Coors, or a Schlitz. But I have learned to appreciate the fine craft of beer making and love a small-batch brew. So on my trip to Greenland, when I heard there was a craft brewery in town, I made a beeline for it.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Ftravel\u002Ffinger-pulling-head-pulling-and-kick-the-seal-122521580652.html\"\u003EFinger Pulling and Kick the Seal &#x2014; Welcome to the Arctic Games!\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E \n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F93fb6d09ed4cf36c50b1cd8100b9a9da95be5f9d.png\" alt=\"Taste-Testing Greenland&#x2019;s Finest Microbrew Beers\" width=\"540\" height=\"304\"\u003E \n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe Godthaab Bryghus brewery is in a building that conveniently also houses a dive bar called Daddy&#x2019;s. While &#x201C;Daddy&#x201D; is a great guy named Gert, the actual brewery is run by Mikael Sorenson, who swears that the beer there is made with glacier ice that is at least 2,000 years old.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;Yes, we have men who go out onto the ice and cut slabs off the glaciers for us and bring them back here for our beer,&#x201D; Sorenson said.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E[Side note: Apparently ice cutting is a big business. Down the street is an ice cream shop that also uses 2,000-year-old ice. &#x201C;Ice cream in Greenland?&#x201D; you may be asking. &#x201C;Isn&#x2019;t it cold enough?&#x201D; No. It&#x2019;s not. Greenland has the second largest ice cream consumption per capita in the world, second only to Finland. Go figure.]\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E \n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"304\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F3a590de53797cb2f646953e3212a190735cb2dff.png\"\u003E \n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EWhile there are no official stats on how much beer is consumed in &#xA0;Nuuk, Greenland&#x2019;s capital, judging by the crowds in the bars and the continual snow, I&#x2019;d say it ranks right up there. And frankly, I can&#x2019;t say I blame them &#x2014; the weather is rough (see previous episode: &#x201C;\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Ftravel\u002Fsnowmageddon-2015-cabin-fever-hits-hard-in-123462240287.html\"\u003ESnowmageddon 2015: Cabin Fever Hits Hard in Greenland\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#x201D;), and the beer is delicious. At the time I visited, there were five beers on tap, including the Musk Ox, the Eric the Red, and the Polar Bear (they like to name the beers after local animals). And here&#x2019;s a tip: While they are all delicious, if you ever find yourself at Daddy&#x2019;s in Nuuk, ask for Gert and Mikael and get them to give you the unfiltered versions of all the beers. They may smell like dirty feet, but they taste like heaven.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Ftravel\u002Fsnowmageddon-2015-cabin-fever-hits-hard-in-123462240287.html\"\u003ESnowmageddon 2015: Cabin Fever Hits Hard in Greenland\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThere is only one problem with the Godthaab Bryghus beer &#x2014; while it is possibly the best beer I have ever tasted (and trust: I have tasted a lot of beer), they don&#x2019;t export. So to get 2,000-year-old glacier-water beer, you have to go to the source. It&#x2019;s worth it. \u003Cbr\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Cb\u003ELet Yahoo Travel inspire you every day. (Photo: iStock\u002FThinkstock)\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EDriving down the Oregon and California coasts it&#x2019;s hard to keep your eyes on the road &#x2014; the scenery is that spectacular. Highways 101 and 1 hug rugged oceanfront cliffs, roll past pastoral farmland, and weave through redwood forests, vineyards, and beach communities.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EAnd yet, epic scenes aren&#x2019;t the only attention grabbers: Animals constantly vied for my attention. And I&#x2019;m not talking about the wander-into-the-middle-of-the-road-and-force-you-to-jam-the-brakes kind either. Here, amid large expanses of natural settings, where I might be the only car for miles and miles, I found myself consistently pulling over to watch sheep grazing, birds migrating and cows&#x2026; well, being cows.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EBeyond these quiet observations, unique opportunities abounded to get up close with the region&#x2019;s awesome animals, like whales and sea lions. While strolling the resort town of Newport, I followed the loud honking to a tiny pier dominated by sea lions. Sea lions are scattered up and down the west coast shoreline, but this is the closest that I got to them. And here&#x2019;s the kicker: I think some of them actually posed for my camera, in between barking, growling and, snuggling with one another.\u003Cstrong\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"Sea lions hanging out on the rocks in Newport, Oregon\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"500\" height=\"331\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002Fbcdb0b6ec8a1e6a11dd7b23195932e3a12be2d85.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cem\u003ESea lions hang out on the rocks (Photo:&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.flickr.com\u002Fphotos\u002Fkightp\u002F7830025514\u002Fin\u002Fphotolist-cVUVMU-dY8kiN-7v5KED-bmd3Yg-bmd3Vv-61Kvqn-cVR9rd-8wH7f2-8wL6Jm-bmd4CK-eZPaLh-61Kun2-bmcxNT-61KueX-985SW5-61KuDi-8GPJq-h6GXkW-61PGG1-61KtP6-8t4jSf-8t1i82-8t4jVW-61Kuvv-61Kv1i-61Ku7k-bAXcdE-bPRQAt-61KvPk-61Kw5a-61KvFg-cVUW9W-61Kwfi-7a64TF-61KuTi-61Kvbe-61PH6Y-61PGrQ-61PEKC-7a9TKW-61Ktxp-61PHzU-61KtYM-7a64Y8-jVGjCc-5yTeUd-8GNkw-d5pyKL-cXYzCb-d5pysw\" target=\"_blank\"\u003EPat Knight\u002FFlickr\u003C\u002Fa\u003E)\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"image\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"359\" height=\"478\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w359\u002Fb3b5f6b94bb987ae7b9b0b7b5b586de1f7297cc4.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cem\u003E(Photo: iStock\u002FThinkstock)\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EPort Orford, Oregon: Dinosaurs\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EI was the oldest visitor without a child to journey back in time at&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.prehistoricgardens.com\u002F\" target=\"_blank\"\u003EPrehistoric Gardens\u003C\u002Fa\u003E &#x2014; but I didn&#x2019;t care.
